## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names the corpus verifier while the theme's real gates are the sources' own checklists, the six-item no-code compatibility checklist, the validation plan, and the prompt regression checklist
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the upgrade doctrine is gate-driven by design, compatibility is checked before recommending, evals validate after upgrading, and each prompt block must prove it addresses an observed regression
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the gates are judgment calls over a specific integration, two reviewers can disagree on whether a fix is prompt-only or needs implementation work
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the gate set defines what must pass before upgrade guidance is trusted and does not automate the judgment
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to adopt the compatibility checklist as the pre-recommendation gate, the validation plan as the post-upgrade gate, and the regression checklist as the prompt-edit gate, with blocked and unknown as legitimate outcomes

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide keys adopt, adapt, and avoid to generic evidence agreement instead of this theme's variables, upgrade class, workflow shape, and whether live verification is available
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine itself grades intervention size by workflow shape, model string only for short bounded prompts, light rewrite for research or tool-heavy flows, blocked when implementation changes loom
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: judging workflow shape is subjective, a minimal visible snippet can hide a tool-heavy host, which the guide addresses by forbidding blocked verdicts on snippet minimalism alone

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds endpoints per batch but not this theme's working unit, one integration's upgrade assessed per focused pass, with usage-site count as the real cost driver
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the workflow inventories every usage site and pairs each with its prompt surface, so effort scales with sites and prompt-surface distance rather than codebase size
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: site-count bounds are estimates, one site with tangled shared templates can outweigh ten clean inline prompts
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds assessment work per session and does not bound the eval runs that validate afterward
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rebound the model around one integration per pass, per-site records as the unit of progress, and the prompting-guide load budgeted when any site needs a rewrite
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the expensive case is the unpairable prompt, hunting a prompt surface that cannot be confidently tied to its usage is unbounded, which is why the doctrine licenses the unknown verdict as the workload escape valve

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the doctrine prescribes level-specific retries, two fallback strategies before declaring no results, escalated-permission retry before asking the user to install, and prompt-level fixes before raising reasoning effort
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: retry ladders assume the failure is transient or steerable, a truly blocked upgrade must exit the ladder rather than climb it
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retrying retrieval and upgrade work, kept alongside the seed's reference-verification retry rules as two labeled layers
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the theme's ladders, empty results get two fallback strategies then an honest report, MCP failures get self-install then escalated retry then a user ask, behavior regressions get prompt blocks before effort increases
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that all three ladders share one shape, cheap self-service retries first, escalation second, honest surrender third, and the doctrine treats the surrender step as a deliverable rather than a failure
